<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9f0d1df4-18c7-454d-8940-a36a42b2a3e9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer4114421529437572454">At 21, Calla hasn’t done a lot of things. She’s never been kissed, never seen the ocean, never gone to an amusement park.   <span id="freeText4114421529437572454" style="display:none">At 21, Calla hasn’t done a lot of things. She’s never been kissed, never seen the ocean, never gone to an amusement park. But growing up, she witnessed some things no child ever should. She still carries the physical and emotional scars of living with a strung-out mother, Mona—secrets she keeps from everyone, including her close circle of college friends.<br /><br />But the safe cocoon Calla has carefully built is shattered when she discovers her mom has stolen her college money and run up a huge credit card debt in her name. Now, Calla has to go back to the small town she thought she'd left behind and clean up her mom’s mess again. Of course, when she arrives at her mother’s bar, Mona is nowhere to be found. Instead, six feet of hotness named Jackson James is pouring drinks and keeping the place humming.<br /><br />Sexy and intense, Jax is in Calla’s business from the moment they meet, giving her a job and helping her search for Mona. And the way he looks at her makes it clear he wants to get horizontal . . . and maybe something more. Before Calla can let him get close, though, she’s got to deal with the pain of the past—and some very bad guys out to mess her up if she doesn’t give them her mom.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Calla is Tessa's friend who was introduced in Be with Me. She was in Tessa's music class with her. Calla is the girl with the scar going down the side<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Calla is Tessa's friend who was introduced in Be with Me. She was in Tessa's music class with her. Calla is the girl with the scar going down the side of her face. She is a nursing student. She told Tessa that she was still a virgin in Be with Me. Jax was not in any of the other stories. He is a new character. I thought Calla was going to get together with Brandon a guy she had a crush on in Be with Me (he was in like two scenes in Be with Me). Jackson is a brand new character. It sounds interesting though.<br /><br />There is a new teaser for Stay with Me where Calla meets Jax. <br /><b>Here is the link:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/happyeverafter/2014/08/14/stay-with-me-excerpt-j-lynn-jennifer-armentrout/14012689/">http://www.usatoday.com/story/happyev...</a><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_846397697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/846397697" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/846397697?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846397697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17312858890072862317"><b>4.5 Stars!!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/587c69f9-ce41-4688-af1d-fd133efcb0e3_zpsc5705a1e.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279747.jpg' alt=' photo 587c69f9-ce41-4688-af1d-fd133efcb0e3_zpsc5705a1e.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>JLA is a master at writing New Adult. She does it so well. <i>Stay with Me</i> is the fourth book in her series and it’s actually one of my favorites. No one can top Cam and his cookies, but Jax was pretty damn close. Holy hot alpha male! This was not only sweet, steamy and funny, but it had some drama, grit and angst, too. <br/><br/>Calla is friends with Teresa who is Cam’s little sister. She’s the quiet one. She has a past that she doesn’t like to talk about. It’s not been an easy life for her a</span>
  <span id="freeText17312858890072862317" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/587c69f9-ce41-4688-af1d-fd133efcb0e3_zpsc5705a1e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279747.jpg" alt=" photo 587c69f9-ce41-4688-af1d-fd133efcb0e3_zpsc5705a1e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>JLA is a master at writing New Adult. She does it so well. <i>Stay with Me</i> is the fourth book in her series and it’s actually one of my favorites. No one can top Cam and his cookies, but Jax was pretty damn close. Holy hot alpha male! This was not only sweet, steamy and funny, but it had some drama, grit and angst, too. <br><br>Calla is friends with Teresa who is Cam’s little sister. She’s the quiet one. She has a past that she doesn’t like to talk about. It’s not been an easy life for her and she’s got the scars to prove it. Calla is on the right track with her life. She’s put her past behind her and is looking forward to her future. She’s determined to achieve her goals. <br><i>
  <blockquote>my goals- the three F’s<br>Finish college. <br>Find a career in the nursing field.<br>Finally reap the benefits of following through on something.</blockquote>
</i> <br>Calla has to focus on the future. Her past is ugly. She doesn't’ want to be anything like the woman who raised her. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/bf62581c-e782-4832-8bce-dfe677b73243_zps1c4d724e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279748.jpg" alt=" photo bf62581c-e782-4832-8bce-dfe677b73243_zps1c4d724e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Things are going right along until Calla’s past comes back to bite her in a big way. After her mom royally screws her by stealing all her college money then doing a disappearing act, she’s stuck going back to the one place she thought she’d never go. Home. <br><br>When she gets to her family’s bar, the last thing she expects to see is a handsome bartender. She hasn’t been here in a while, but still. Guys like that do not work at places like this. Jax and Calla are drawn to each other immediately. Jax knows all the bad things Calla’s mother is into, and is determined to get her out of that town, or at the very least keep her safe while she’s here. <br><i>
  <blockquote> “I want to make sure you’re safe since you’re staying for... however long. And being here by yourself isn’t safe, so I’m going to make it safe for you.”</blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/474e6c0f-d535-494e-bb65-e0a1e6f0e7b7_zpsf0f72669.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279749.jpg" alt=" photo 474e6c0f-d535-494e-bb65-e0a1e6f0e7b7_zpsf0f72669.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What can I even say about Jax? Jax felt like a mini-new adult KA alpha. Which is a compliment in the highest regards. As much as I did like Calla, Jax completely made this book! <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> “I like you, Calla. Yeah, I’ve only known you a couple of days. But you’ve made me laugh. I can also tell you’re nice and sweet when you wanna be. I think you’re cute as hell and you make me hard. You’ve made me hard a couple of times in the last seventy-some-odd hours and I gotta say that’s not a bad thing. I want to fuck you, and all I need to want to do that with you is to like you. It’s really not that hard to get from point A to point C on that, honey.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Jax is sexy, he is sweet and the way he treats Calla made me melt. When he looks at her, he doesn’t see the scarred girl that she sees. He sees beauty. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“I used to be really pretty. See? I used-” <br>“There is no ‘used’ to be. You’re really fucking pretty now.”</blockquote>
</i><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/45939437-cf8a-4a2b-a60e-ed7f5de30594_zps504dd407.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279750.jpg" alt=" photo 45939437-cf8a-4a2b-a60e-ed7f5de30594_zps504dd407.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I found Calla to be a very likable character. She’s had an extremely hard life, and she’s chosen a better path. I love the way Jax was able to get her to open up, to try new things. It was also fantastic to catch up with the rest of the crew. There were quite a few Cam, Avery, Jase and Teresa scenes! <br><br><i>Stay with Me</i> is not only a beautiful romance between two scarred people, it’s a tale of accepting yourself. There was steam, emotional parts, sweet parts, drama, and lots of action! It was one heck of a ride. So why not 5? There really is just one main reason it didn’t hit the 5 star mark for me. It was a little on the longish side, and although most of the story was fast paced, there were a few parts that lagged. Overall- I found this to be an endearing story and it’s one I would recommend to new adult fans!<br><br> <a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/81d0279e-4569-4054-8b85-6b8e08f6f339_zpsb135de83.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411808736i/11279751.jpg" alt=" photo 81d0279e-4569-4054-8b85-6b8e08f6f339_zpsb135de83.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17312858890072862317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1954392285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954392285" />
    <a title="KAS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20691061-kas"><img alt="KAS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472348331p2/20691061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1954392285?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KAS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KAS" href="/user/show/20691061-kas">KAS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954392285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14846979906615995999"><br/>Once I start a series I love, I am like a dog with a bone. I can't let it go until I've read them all. Calla was introduced in book two, "Be With Me." She is Teresa's college roommate and friend. 'Friend' being the operative word, as in high school she was never referred to as anyone's 'girlfriend,' because no guy would ever ask her out. She is twenty-one years old, and has yet to experience her first kiss.<br/><br/>Right out of the gate, Calla had my heart. She was the girl in high school whom classmates</span>
  <span id="freeText14846979906615995999" style="display:none"><br />Once I start a series I love, I am like a dog with a bone. I can't let it go until I've read them all. Calla was introduced in book two, "Be With Me." She is Teresa's college roommate and friend. 'Friend' being the operative word, as in high school she was never referred to as anyone's 'girlfriend,' because no guy would ever ask her out. She is twenty-one years old, and has yet to experience her first kiss.<br /><br />Right out of the gate, Calla had my heart. She was the girl in high school whom classmates enjoyed teasing. You see, there is a very noticeable scar that runs the length of her left cheek. It has been there since age ten after a horrific event which changes her and her families life forever. Needing to get away from it all, she enters a college nursing program hours away from home.<br /><br />Only one year left until graduating from college, Calla learns her savings account has been drained, and she knows just who the culprit is. Mona. Her drugged out, drunken excuse of a mother. Calla packs up and heads back home hoping she can at least recover some of the money stolen from her. She walks into the bar her mother owns only to learn she left two weeks ago, crazed out of her mind, and hasn't been seen or heard from since. Standing behind the bar to greet her is the hottest, sexiest man she has ever met. The way he grins and laughs totally does her in. Surprisingly, shocking her actually, he asks her out. She can hardly believe this eye-candy hunk genuinely seems attracted to her. <br /><br />Jax is one smooth, p.u.r.e. to the core male. Confidence runs through his veins and he has the art of flirting down pat. 'Bossy' could also be his middle name. He has been working behind the bar of Mona's for two years, when one night, in walks a very pretty woman and sits down at as his bar. Yeah, he sees the scar running down her cheek, but all he really sees is how hot she is. Only problem is her mother is Mona. Mona is trouble, and since trouble follows trouble, he knows Calla is in danger if word gets out she is back home.<br /><br />Jax warns Calla to leave town! She doesn't listen to him! Unfortunately, she should have!<br /><br />If anyone ever needed a knight in shining armor, it is Calla, and Jax makes it his mission in life to be that knight and a whole lot more.<br /><br />While this book is much longer in length than the others so far in this series, I was never bored. I was frustrated at times, but was also invested in both Calla and Jax's relationship to keep me turning the pages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14846979906615995999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846357657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8498988337743050758"><b> 5 Staying Stars! </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/staywithmecollage.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411632345i/11259023._SX540_.png' alt=' photo staywithmecollage.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I love J. Lynn. I love Jennifer L. Armentrout. Doesn't matter what name she's writing under, I almost always love her books. Stay With Me is no exception.<br/><br/>Calla has a problem. She needs to finish her final year of college to obtain her nursing degree, and everything was going along fine. Until her mom cleaned out her college fund. And then took out over $100,000 worth of credit card debt in her name. Yikes!<br/><br/>Calla returns home to the town and bar she thought she'd never see ag</span>
  <span id="freeText8498988337743050758" style="display:none"><b> 5 Staying Stars! </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/staywithmecollage.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411632345i/11259023._SX540_.png" alt=" photo staywithmecollage.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I love J. Lynn. I love Jennifer L. Armentrout. Doesn't matter what name she's writing under, I almost always love her books. Stay With Me is no exception.<br><br>Calla has a problem. She needs to finish her final year of college to obtain her nursing degree, and everything was going along fine. Until her mom cleaned out her college fund. And then took out over $100,000 worth of credit card debt in her name. Yikes!<br><br>Calla returns home to the town and bar she thought she'd never see again, and there she meets Jax. Jax is the sexy bartender working at her mother's bar, Mona's, and he's interested in Calla. Way interested. Together, the two of them search for Calla's mom who has gone missing, and along the way, find a connection in each other.<br><br>I thoroughly enjoyed reading this book. I did a giant happy dance when I got home from work and the Amazon package was sitting there with this puppy inside. <br><br><a href="http://reactiongifs.com/?p=20608" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400496990ra/9682774.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I started reading immediately and didn't put this one down for the next 24 hours or so. Why 24 hours? Well I have to work some time people! That and this book was surprisingly long. Almost 450 pages of awesomeness!<br><br>Calla is a heroine that I adore. Everything she's been through has caused her to cut herself off from life and people, in an effort to protect herself. I found her to be so brave with all of the trials and tribulations she went up against in this book, and holy shit did she have more than a plateful in this book. It was almost disturbing how much the author liked to kick Calla when she was down. Enough already! We get it, shitty things happen to Calla. Back off JLA!<br><br>Jax.... oh Jax. ***giant sigh***. <br><br><a href="http://reactiongifs.com/?p=21139" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403010552ra/10025572.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was a man to bring home to mom. (Well not Calla's mom, but you know). He reminded me a bit of Kristen Ashley's alpha males. He didn't let anyone push him around, and more importantly he didn't let anyone push Calla around and stood up for her time and time again. Yes, he messed up a little along the way, but those were understandable misunderstandings (does that even make sense?). <br><br>The first book will probably always be my favorite, so that's still the best one in the series. But Stay With Me runs a close 2nd place, because I'm still recovering from the whiplash that was Be With Me.<br><br>My only complaint was sometimes JLA got a little too hip with her descriptions, if that's possible. It no longer became cute to read things that didn't even make sense. Like "Holy granola bar". Um, what? Where the F*** did that come from? It's cute a couple of times, but it happened quite a bit. Too much, but that's just my opinion.<br><br>Can we have a Reece and Roxy story please? </span>
  <a data-text-id="8498988337743050758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1804194217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804194217" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804194217?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19407085-stay-with-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804194217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5255226991236274808"><blockquote>
  <i>“You with me?” <br/>Remembering him saying that before, our first time, I nodded and whispered, “Yes.” <br/>He kissed me again. “Then stay with me.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This wasn't better than Wait for You, but it was better than Be with Me. The problem I had with this book was Jax, but later on. I enjoyed his character in the beginning and was literally in love with him, wishing guys like him existed in my world, but then I didn't feel anything for him and he actually got to the point where he got on my nerves and all I </span>
  <span id="freeText5255226991236274808" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“You with me?” <br />Remembering him saying that before, our first time, I nodded and whispered, “Yes.” <br />He kissed me again. “Then stay with me.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This wasn't better than Wait for You, but it was better than Be with Me. The problem I had with this book was Jax, but later on. I enjoyed his character in the beginning and was literally in love with him, wishing guys like him existed in my world, but then I didn't feel anything for him and he actually got to the point where he got on my nerves and all I wanted to do was punch him and yell "really Jax?" because honestly, he deserved a punch.<br /><br /><i>Stay with Me</i> is the third novel in J. Lynn's series, <i>Wait for You</i>. It can be read as a stand alone. As a matter of fact, all of them can, but I prefer to read them all in order to learn about each character and to see if they will make an appearance in the next book. Stay with Me is about Calla, who was mentioned quite a few times in Be with Me, the story about Jase and Teresa. This time, it's about Calla and Jax. Calla is a 21-year-old college student that literally has done nothing. She's never been to New York (oh who am I to judge, neither have I!), never been to an amusement park, never been to the beach, and <b>never been kissed.</b> She's in college, studying nursing, wanting to become a nurse in the future, but when she finds out her mom has stolen her college fund, she realizes she is in debt and doesn't know what to do. She's hoping to find a solution when she goes back to her mom's bar, <i>Mona's,</i> with the scars and the horrible memories of her past caused by her mother. When she gets to the bar, she doesn't spot the solution she was hoping to find, but she does spot a 6 foot tall and hot bartender, Jackson James, pouring drinks and running the bar.<br /><br />Knowing Calla needs to make up for her money being stolen by her own mom, she takes a job at her mother's bar, being given the job by Jax himself, even helping her find her mother. Jackson and Calla might be able to develop a sexy and intense relationship, but her past is stopping her at times from getting too close to him. As the two get to know each other more leading her and Jax from strangers to "friends with benefits," there are some bad guys looking for Calla and even daring to threaten her and mess up her life if she doesn't tell them where her mom is. The problem is, Calla doesn't know where her mom is and what happened.<br /><br />The reason I put <b>friends with benefits</b> in quotation marks is because that's what Calla's and Jax's relationship felt like. They didn't even know each other, and right off the bat, Jax was telling her he liked her and wanted to fuck her. Of course, Calla being the innocent girl she is having the hots for Jax, she didn't care and the three words would just repeat in her mind because wanted that as well, even without admitting it. They didn't even know each other, and Jax had told her everything he really wanted to do <i>to and with her.</i> The problem I had with this was the relationship between the two. The two characters were very different, and not in a good way. There were really <i>no connections</i> between the two and the chemistry was not there until later on, as the novel was finishing. There wasn't any chemistry when they first started dating and there wasn't a hint of cute romance anywhere to be seen. As I'm reading every book in this series, the books tend to get worse and worse or are just not my thing.<br /><br />Like I said, this wasn't better than Wait for You, but it was 1-star better than Be with You. Unlike Be with You, Jax didn't reject Calla, but he also didn't <i>show his love for her</i> either. He ran off at times, but not in the way Jase did with Tess. He would tell Calla she is beautiful and that he is in love with her in every way, but then he would be having one of the girl's he used to "hook up with" giving him a breast examination. The worst thing is that Calla's friends not only met but saw Jax for the first time when he was being given that breast examination. Calla didn't get over that and she brought it up once or twice, but I really didn't blame her. Calla having her friends there to surprise her and be there for her but meeting her "boyfriend" in the worst place possible would honestly be embarrassing! Think about it: <i>You met up with your friends so they can meet your so-called boyfriend, but when you noticed them and they asked about him, you turn to his side and notice he's talking to a girl you really don't like and the other thing is, she is giving him a breast examination. The other thing is,</i> <i>
  <b>he isn't fucking complaining!</b>
</i> Jax sounded hot, to be honest, being the tall bartender with his perfectly shaped and sharp jaw and perfect brown eyes that would look like the dreamy chocolate (whatever the fuck that is) and would basically capture a girls heart in an instant, but in reality, he took everything way too quick, didn't show his love for Calla in the correct way, and was plain as gross at times admitting he wants to fuck Calla. I mean, I said this once and I'll say it again, but you can't disagree. I mean, c'mon. The guy should've met Calla first and <i>really met her</i> before shoving his peepee inside her. <b>Oh boy.</b> I know he has a past as well, but again, it's so different. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[His sister died in a car crash and when Calla was in the hospital because she was shot, it brought some memories to him, ending up blaming himself for it and for Calla getting hurt. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Sure, I felt bad, but other times, I wanted to punch him in the face because of the way he acted <b>with</b> Calla.<br /><br />Moving on, Calla, on the other hand, was a character I enjoyed without complaints. The girl has literally been through a lot thanks to her mom, and she really wasn't planning on changing that. Her mom is a bitch, it's all learned in later throughout the novel, but she is. She abandoned her child and left her and then decided to steal her <b>college money</b> with her name only to leave her <b>in debt</b> and having to work at her <b>own bar</b> with her so-called boyfriend. The problem is since everyone knows her mom in that town and that bar, then can go there an insult Calla right in her face, which is sad. It's so sad how her mom literally doesn't love her because she hasn't moved on <b>from her past</b> but the thing is, her past <b>is gone.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Calla's siblings died, and her mom won't get over it. She told Calla that she has been through a lot and that her babies have died, but then, Calla is there. Is she a dead baby to her mom? I guess so! Also, her father is gone too and her mom seems to give zero fucks about it and doesn't even care what her daughter has been through. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Her mom was just a bitch to her and is the reason Calla had to live the awful life she lived through. She saw things she didn't want to see as a child and now that she is old enough to live her life on her own and make a difference, but there were people and things in the way of her doing that <b>thanks to her mom.</b> Luckily, it's all over and the people going after her mom are done, not blaming, but giving Calla shit about it. Thanks to Jax (sort of), her life became a little easier and thanks to him, she's been able to move on a little from the past. He found her to be beautiful with her scars and didn't mind them but instead was proud of her for being brave and carrying scars with her. I mean, scars can mean something. They either mean something stupid, or they are there to represent something. Calla was ashamed to carry them, but then she found herself not bothering to hide them from Jax and that was something I liked from both. He didn't mind them and found her to be beautiful and strong with them while she wasn't ashamed anymore to carry them for reasons. <br /><br />I did say he told Calla he liked her straight off the bat, but I didn't mention what I <b>actually liked about him.</b> I was glad he was another one of those male leads that take their time with the girl and makes sure they get to know them. There was a time where Calla was drunk <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for the first time with Tequila <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and she said and did stupid things. I mean, everyone who is drunk in NA novels do. In real life too, right? (I don't live with a drunk family so I wouldn't know). She tried doing things with Jax and she tried kissing him, but he backed away and pushed her away. I'm not the bad person here, but I'm glad he did. The reason I'm glad is because <i>Calla was the one to always argue with Jax because they didn't know each other and he had asked her out (which is stupid because that's kind of the point of a date, right? Getting to know each other?)</i> <b>yet</b> she was trying to be all up on him, trying to kiss him when he didn't want to <b>because</b> he wanted to be her <i>first kiss</i> in a better way, not when she was drunk. She was drunk, so she didn't know what she was doing, but Jax was patient enough to push her away and tell her what he really wanted to do--<b>go out with her and get to know her.</b> That was about it, actually. Other than that, there wasn't anything. There were times where he was there to save her and help her, but other than that, there wasn't anything else. He wasn't a swoon-worthy character in my opinion.<br /><br />Calla wasn't that different than the other females in the previous books. She also tries running from her past but not being able to until <i>she meets a guy.</i> I'm quite glad these novels have a connection with everything--the characters are friends, the plots are all similar in ways, and the every character has something similar to share. <br /><br />This wasn't my favorite, and I really hate how I enjoyed the beginning of it but then it got to the point where I was done with Jax and his bullshit. I wish Calla's character and personality were different. She actually didn't have a good one, in my opinion. It really wasn't there. Jax did a lot for her, and it was too much. She could've been the girl to step away for a while and figure out things on her own, but she relayed her nonexisting trust on him which wasn't the best choice for her. J. Lynn disappointed e with this one, once again, and I only hope this doesn't continue. I was really looking forward to this one, especially because of Calla. We're told she's someone who is 21 and has literally done nothing. I knew Jax would get involved in that, but I actually thought <b>she would get those completed</b> but instead, I got a lot of drama and overused sex scenes that weren't my favorite. I mean, sex in NA books isn't my favorite, which I've said over and over again, but these were the kind where all Jax really wanted to do was <b>fuck Calla.</b> She had just solved something, and he was like "okay, I want to be in you. Now." and I was like "boy she just got out of a problem let her breathe happiness for a minute." <i>*Sigh.*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5255226991236274808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_834032750" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/834032750" />
    <a title="Maida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5808311-maida"><img alt="Maida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401945746p2/5808311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/834032750?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maida" href="/user/show/5808311-maida">Maida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19407085-stay-with-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=series-trilogies">series-trilogies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=socio-economic">socio-economic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=substance-abuse">substance-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=moral-dilemmas">moral-dilemmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=socio-psychology">socio-psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=sexual-psychophysiological">sexual-psychophysiological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=dysfunctional-individuals-families">dysfunctional-individuals-families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5808311-maida?shelf=trauma">trauma</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834032750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5759110175460701851"><i>Full review to come when— or rather *if*— I ever recover from the atrocious writing....</i> Not since the 3rd grade have I read a novel which utilized such a limited vocabulary & word set. The word "holy" appears in this novel <b>43 times</b>— possibly more times than it appears in a standard Presbyterian hymnal. The words "baby" and "ass" are each used <b>74 times.</b> (I actually began highlighting these <b>overly used & abused</b> words & expressions after coming across the word "ass" 7 times on a single page & 3 tim</span>
  <span id="freeText5759110175460701851" style="display:none"><i>Full review to come when— or rather *if*— I ever recover from the atrocious writing....</i> Not since the 3rd grade have I read a novel which utilized such a limited vocabulary &amp; word set. The word "holy" appears in this novel <b>43 times</b>— possibly more times than it appears in a standard Presbyterian hymnal. The words "baby" and "ass" are each used <b>74 times.</b> (I actually began highlighting these <b>overly used &amp; abused</b> words &amp; expressions after coming across the word "ass" 7 times on a single page &amp; 3 times within the same short 4-sentence-long paragraph).... However, the real doozy is the following: The word "stomach" appears in this novel a WHOPPING <b>90 times</b>!!! <i>WHY?</i> I'm really not quite sure, since the parts of the story that should repeatedly mention the word "stomach" occur only towards the novel's end. I do have my theories, however, &amp; I'll expound on these theories *if* I can ever muster the will-power to write a full review. <br /><br /><b>In short: This novel is written on a 3rd-grade reading level. For a novel that is supposed to cover some very serious themes, the writing is just way too immature. I was under the impression that I was picking up a novel about a 21-year old woman. Instead, the heroine's inner monologue resembled that of a prepubescent girl, &amp; I found much of the hero's behavior towards the heroine troubling, cruel &amp; unhealthy.</b><br /><br /><b>*0.5/5 stars*</b><br /><br /><br /><i>Status Update from 9/23/14:</i> Only 10% of the way through, &amp; I'm already considering waving the white flag. Surrendering. DNF'ing. The opening chapters make me want to slam my head against the bedside table— let's call it "self-induced amnesia"— whatever it takes to black out everything that I've read up until this point.... I sympathize with the character Calla; I truly do. I admire her tenacity &amp; her resolve. She's led a very difficult life, &amp; in that sense, I honestly <i>CAN</i> empathize..... The entire novel is told solely from Calla's POV, &amp; although I do respect this character, I'm doubtful that I can spend 450 pages inside her head, all the while keeping my own sanity intact in the process.<br /><br />The writing in the opening paragraphs leaves a lot to be desired. IMO, it's the weakest writing that I've seen thus far from JLA. There’s something that happens very early in the novel— something that the author uses as a vehicle to move the plot forward. I don't find these turn of events the least bit believable. It's over-the-top drama at best, &amp; it just doesn’t make sense for this sort of thing to happen to Calla— a 21-year old woman who is estranged from her entire family &amp; who is therefore self-sufficient, independent, intelligent, driven &amp; highly responsible. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If you were Calla— a legal adult who has been long-estranged from your family... and if you were completely self-sufficient &amp; putting yourself through college via your waitressing job &amp; a few student loans... and if you just happened to have an alcoholic &amp; drug-addicted mother whom you haven't seen in years— a mother whom you repeatedly refer to as "dead" whenever anyone asks— would you allow this mother access to your checking &amp; savings accounts? The same checking &amp; savings accounts where you deposit your wages— the same checking account that pays your university tuition &amp; your rent? Would you allow your mother (a woman whom you repeatedly refer to as "dead" &amp; someone whom you have't seen in years) access to a bank account that you rely on for your livelihood, knowing fully well that this woman is alcohol &amp; drug addicted &amp; that she can wipe out your funds at any time, thereby leaving you with NOTHING. NO college tuition. NO money to pay the rent. NO money for your monthly car payments. NOTHING. NADA. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Would you do it? NO?!? I didn't think so... and herein lies my problem with this story. The plot device moving the storyline forward is illogical, nonsensical &amp; asinine. A person has to be extremely daft to allow such a thing happen, &amp; I certainly don't believe that Calla is daft. It's the <i>unbelievability factor</i> that's turning me off more than anything. SORRY, JLA, BUT I'M JUST NOT DRINKING THE KOOL AID. :(<br /><br />Clarification of the spoiler above:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The heroine (Calla) doesn't come straight out &amp; say that her mom has unfettered access to her bank account. Her exact words are as follows: <i>"This might not be a giant fuckup by the bank and the college. This could very well be seriously happening. Oh my God. Because there was someone other than me who had the means to get access to that account—one person who was virtually dead to me, so virtually that I behaved as if she were dead.... I knew it had been my own flesh and blood that had cleared me out, my own mother—my hocked up on pills, and most likely drunk off her ass, mother who my closest friends believed was dead. In a way, that hadn’t been too far from the truth. A terrible lie, but I hadn’t talked to her in ages..."</i> The story only gets worse from there. Calla then finds out that her mother has taken out $100,000 worth of loans &amp; credit cards under Calla's name. Calla's mother couldn't have pulled this whole thing off overnight. It's something that must have happened gradually over time— another aspect of the storyline which I find improbable. Calla is financially independent &amp; alone. She does everything for herself. She applies for her own apartments, she recently bought her own car, etc... which means that she's accessed her credit report on more than a few occasions over the past year or two. Calla is the kind of person who keeps a tight leash on things; she's the kind of person who knows how much money is in her checking &amp; savings accounts to the decimal point. So how could she not have known that someone took out over $100,000 in credit cards &amp; loans under her name? How is it even possible that Calla could be approved for such high credit limits? I know that identity theft is a common problem in our society &amp; that it can happen to any of us. But it's the circumstances surrounding the identity theft in this novel that I take issue with. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5759110175460701851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/809418905" />
    <a title="C.K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20534694-c-k"><img alt="C.K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496441314p2/20534694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/809418905?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.K." href="/user/show/20534694-c-k">C.K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer809418905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6833517005762228129"><br/><br/><br/><b> Here is the link to a Sneak Preview of Stay with Me (the first 7 chapters:</b><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.facebook.com/NewAdultBooks/app_196263097093013?ref=page_internal'>https://www.facebook.com/NewAdultBook...</a><br/><br/><b> Here is a link to chapter 1 and 2 of Stay with Me U.K. version</b><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://romancefestival.wordpress.com/2014/06/08/exclusive-stay-with-me-cover-reveal-chapters-1-2-j-lynn-romance14/'>http://romancefestival.wordpress.com/...</a><br/><br/><br/><b>New Teaser with Jax/Calla!</b><br/> <br/><b>Jax caught my arm. “You’re forgetting something.”<br/> <br/>“What?”<br/> <br/>The half grin appeared as he turned his hand around my arm, tugging me toward him. I bit down on my lip as I stumbled forward, having no idea what he was about. I got close to him, close enough tha</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6833517005762228129" style="display:none"><br /><br /><br /><b> Here is the link to a Sneak Preview of Stay with Me (the first 7 chapters:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/NewAdultBooks/app_196263097093013?ref=page_internal">https://www.facebook.com/NewAdultBook...</a><br /><br /><b> Here is a link to chapter 1 and 2 of Stay with Me U.K. version</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://romancefestival.wordpress.com/2014/06/08/exclusive-stay-with-me-cover-reveal-chapters-1-2-j-lynn-romance14/">http://romancefestival.wordpress.com/...</a><br /><br /><br /><b>New Teaser with Jax/Calla!</b><br /> <br /><b>Jax caught my arm. “You’re forgetting something.”<br /> <br />“What?”<br /> <br />The half grin appeared as he turned his hand around my arm, tugging me toward him. I bit down on my lip as I stumbled forward, having no idea what he was about. I got close to him, close enough that when he reached down to a cubbyhole, his arm brushed my thigh.<br /> <br />“Got to wear an apron when you’re out there.”<br /> <br />My brows rose as I stared at the half apron. “Seriously?”<br /> <br />He jerked his chin at Pearl. I sighed when I saw she had one tied around her waist, and then snatched it from him.“Whatever.”<br /> <br />“It goes great with your shirt.”<br /> <br />I rolled my eyes.<br /> <br />Jax laughed. “Let me help.”<br /> <br />“The last time I checked, I can tie an apron without—” I gaped at him. Somehow theapron was back in his hand and his other hand landed on my hip, startling me. “What are you doing?”<br /> <br />“Helping you out.” He bent his head toward my left ear, and I immediately turned my cheek. “Jumpy?” he asked.<br /> <br />I shook my head, finding that I had no idea how to form syllables, and that was embarrassing.<br /> <br />Without saying a word, he turned me around so my back was to his front, and then he slipped an arm between his waist and mine. I didn’t dare move.<br /> <br />“You can breathe, you know.” His arm trailed across my lower stomach, setting off a chain of flutters, as he spread the apron.<br /> <br />“I’m breathing,” I forced out.<br /> <br />Amusement colored his tone. “You sure about that, honey?”<br /> <br />“Yeah.”<br /> <br />Pearl entered the bar just then, carrying a tray of clean glasses. She arched her brows inour direction. “Getting hands-on, Jackie boy?”<br /> <br />“Jackie boy?” I mumbled.<br /> <br />Jax chuckled not too far from my ear. “Tying knots is hard.”</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Here is a Teaser I saw for Stay with Me: <br /><br />“Already explained that, honey, but I’ll explain something else to you. When I want something, I go for it. Life is way too damn short to live any other way. And I want to get to know you better,” Those lashes lowered one more time, his gaze tracking to my lips like they were some kind of mecca. “Yeah, I want to definitely get to know you better.”~Jennifer Armentrout, Stay with Me</b>
</i> <br /><br /><b>TEASER 2</b><br /><b>Here is the Link to another teaser when Jax and Calla first meet and it is quite the introduction:<b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://avonromance.com/post/excerpt-reveal-stay-with-me-by-jennifer-l-armentrout-writing-as-j-lynn">http://avonromance.com/post/excerpt-r...</a><br /><br /><b>This is the same excerpt at another site:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/happyeverafter/2014/08/14/stay-with-me-excerpt-j-lynn-jennifer-armentrout/14012689/">http://www.usatoday.com/story/happyev...</a><br /><br /><b>Teaser</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JenniferLArmentrout#!/JenniferLArmentrout/photos/a.286761674758735.51175.285190961582473/531351476966419/?type=1">https://www.facebook.com/JenniferLArm...</a><br /><br /><br />I thought Brandon and Calla were going to get a story but this Jax guy sounds interesting and the teasers have all been good.<br /><br /><b>In case anyone doesn't know. Britt/Ollie have a short story called <i>Believe in Me</i> that is feature in the <i>Anthology Fifty First Times</i>. It came out on February 25th. Ollie and Britts story was really good and not filled with drama. There were some other good stories in the Anthology. I really liked Under the Seryn Moon and Daylight as well. <br /><br />Here is the link on Goodreads:</b><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18513487-fifty-first-times">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a><br /><br /><br /><b>Here is the Link on Amazon:</b><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/Fifty-First-Times-Adult-Anthology-ebook/dp/B00F8P3A36/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1392304508&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=Fifty+first+times">http://www.amazon.com/Fifty-First-Tim...</a></b></b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853455404?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer853455404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9794181500470816005"><b> 4 Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411850662i/11289275._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Calla had the perfect life until a fire destroyed her and her family. While the physical scars are obvious, no one knows about the mental scars she keeps hidden. While she has met some great people she calls friends she has never opened up about her past, in fact she has been lying about it. Although, she feels guilty lying to her friends the most important thing is her three F’s:<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Finish college.<br/>Find a career in the nursing field. <br/>Finally reap the benefits of following through on some</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9794181500470816005" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411850662i/11289275._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Calla had the perfect life until a fire destroyed her and her family. While the physical scars are obvious, no one knows about the mental scars she keeps hidden. While she has met some great people she calls friends she has never opened up about her past, in fact she has been lying about it. Although, she feels guilty lying to her friends the most important thing is her three F’s:<br><br><b>
  <i>"Finish college.<br>Find a career in the nursing field. <br>Finally reap the benefits of following through on something.”</i>
</b><br><br>No she hasn’t a boyfriend, a first kiss, or been drunk, but she is on track to complete the F’s. At the end of the Spring semester her world is blown apart again when she is asked to meet with Financial Aid, and learns all of her money is gone and her check bounced. Deciding she must go home to find what is going on with her strung out mother, she returns home after three years and meets Jax. <br><br>Jax is working at Mona’s, the bar owned by Calla’s mother, when she meets him. He is the definition of hot, and doesn’t seem to be put off by the scars on her face. Not knowing how to treat a guy when is so blatantly pursing her, she ignores it. <br><br>Calla is on a mission, she needs to find her mom and find out what to do for her senior year. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411850662i/11289276._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have loved this series and I was so excited for this installment. <br><br>I loved Calla and her inner thoughts, I loved that she was real, and I really loved that she calmed herself down and thought things out rationally. Typically the female character will drive me crazy obsessing about things or running away, but Calla actually had moments she wanted to run but stayed because she knew it was the smart thing to do. I really liked Jax. I loved the way he made Calla feel, and I loved the sexy times they had - J. Lynn writes some pretty hot scenes. <br><br>So why not 5 stars? Well, this one felt pretty long to me, it dragged in some places and some things didn’t feel necessary. I can’t go into too much detail on the scenes that didn’t feel necessary, without giving away spoilers, but I think after reading it most can guess. <b>Overall, I thoroughly enjoyed this and recommend it and the series for others. </b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411850662i/11289277._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And just because: <b>
  <i>"Oh my God, guys that read were like unicorns. They only existed in fairy tales”<br></i>
</b></span>

  <span id="freeText15763469487027286060" style="display:none">I so want to rant because i so need too... but first things first. I LOVE THIS SERIES. And I loved Calla &amp; Jax's story. I couldn't wait to get Calla's story. And dang did I get one. Calla hasn't had many first times. Never had a kiss, never fell in love, and never went to an amusement park. Never saw a beach. Never had anyone 'touch' her. I could keep on going....<br>To say she's had a rough past would actually be kind. She's had a tragic past, nothing pretty about it at all. She's ready to face the past when her mom does the ultimate unthinkable to her. When she gets back home to where she grew up, she realizes that things are worse than she anticipated. This is when she meets Jax, the guy running her moms bar. This guy instantly catches her attention, the man that makes her feel things for the very first time in her life. As things starts to grow between them, and when Jax makes it clear that he doesn’t only want her as a friend, things will get even more confusing for her. This story, gosh my heart broke for Calla. Like seriously the things that happened to her, good lord... how much can the poor girl take. And seriously that bi*ch Miss Poconos Aimee Grant, with an i and two e's. Seriously <br><a href="http://s1067.photobucket.com/user/grayanncam/media/Mobile%20Uploads/2016-11/444826D5-C492-4860-BA42-4A478A8ABFE4_zpsys5xcwky.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>I can't begin to list the things that happen to Calla &amp; Jax. But at the end of this roller coaster ride, I definitely can not wait to get more to this couple in the future books of this series. Love that this book gave us yet another amazing couple. <br><a href="http://s1067.photobucket.com/user/grayanncam/media/Mobile%20Uploads/2016-11/E80F3C53-DAB1-4213-A70A-AF671F4E7FC0_zpsvtmr1lrq.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer8949467703595867115"><u>
  <b>Review on January 28th, 2017</b>
</u><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"There's something about that...it drew me in, Calla. Fuck. I fell for you before you even knew my name."</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>Stay with Me</i> is the love story of Jax and Calla; oddly, they haven't shown up in the previous instalments in the series. Calla is actually Avery and Cam's college friend while Jax is a total stranger in the beginning of the book. What makes this story different from other sequels in the saga is that Jax has the most unbelievable secret in his mind and when </span>
  <span id="freeText8949467703595867115" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Review on January 28th, 2017</b>
</u><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"There's something about that...it drew me in, Calla. Fuck. I fell for you before you even knew my name."</i>
</blockquote><br /><i>Stay with Me</i> is the love story of Jax and Calla; oddly, they haven't shown up in the previous instalments in the series. Calla is actually Avery and Cam's college friend while Jax is a total stranger in the beginning of the book. What makes this story different from other sequels in the saga is that Jax has the most unbelievable secret in his mind and when it's revealed, everything has changed.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Like I said, you're safe with me. Whenever. Seriously. Whatever you want to explore, you'll always be safe with me."</i>
</blockquote><br />In order not to spoil you guys, I won't say much about their relationship because the entire plot is all about revealing the truth. <br />The only thing I must remind you is that when you're at about <b>CHAPTER 33,</b> (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Jax rushes to the hotel room where Calla escapes to and pours his heart thoroughly in front of her friends <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) <b>PLEASE DO REMEMBER LISTENING TO <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-2U0Ivkn2Ds" rel="nofollow noopener">Say Something by A Great Big World ft. Christina Aguilera</a>!!!!!!</b> That's the first song coming to mind and the specific scene fits the lyrics flawlessly. It's probably the best portrait of the song I've ever seen. <br /><br />Last but not least, just because I skip many delicious details on Jalla's story doesn't mean it's not worth reading. So please, whether you like Cam&amp;Avery, Jase&amp;Tess, or other couples in this series, <b>you don't want to miss this one!!!</b> Jax and Calla's story touches my heart deeply and I'll never forget them.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>The circumstances sucked and were crazy, but I did have my mom to thank for this--for Jax. Our relationship turned out to be a very bright silver lining in a sad, dark cloud.</i>
</blockquote><br />What are you waiting for? Go pick it up right now! <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Instant review on December 9th, 2016</b>
</u><br />Okay. This is official. IT'S THE BEST BOOK IN THE SERIES SO FAR AND I CAN'T EVEN.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8949467703595867115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2360954175086487233">2 DISAPPOINTING STARS<br/><br/>I'm the odd one out on this book. <br/><br/>This is the least favorite of the series for me, it felt too long--I skimmed several times--too laced with slang and the heroine was annoying. The best thing about this book? Jackson James. He was a great hero and almost seemed too perfect but he made the book for me--aside from the fact he was a very KA hero, not a bad thing but not JLA.<br/>Calla was ok, if I looked past her tendency to say, "holy"**insert slang**. Holy shit on a cracker was a </span>
  <span id="freeText2360954175086487233" style="display:none">2 DISAPPOINTING STARS<br /><br />I'm the odd one out on this book. <br /><br />This is the least favorite of the series for me, it felt too long--I skimmed several times--too laced with slang and the heroine was annoying. The best thing about this book? Jackson James. He was a great hero and almost seemed too perfect but he made the book for me--aside from the fact he was a very KA hero, not a bad thing but not JLA.<br />Calla was ok, if I looked past her tendency to say, "holy"**insert slang**. Holy shit on a cracker was a popular one for her and that's alright if it's sporadic but she said things like that too often making her look immature and silly. I completely empathized with her issues and her past, she wasn't always annoying. But she was a bit too much with her gasping over anything Jax said. <br /><br />Heroines that do stupid things when it's obvious to everyone and their dog it's stupid, really bother me. Coming home to deal with the huge debt her mom had left her was the beginning of her life changing. But refusing to see that she needed help at first considering her childhood home was essentially a drug house, was downright childish. She did improve mind you, so that's good. But the book was too long and the ending was resolved a little conveniently. After all the stuff that happened and all the drama, things tied up too perfectly. And it wasn't realistic at all. <br /><br />And although I really liked Jax, the way he dealt <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with Aimee, letting her touch him and then almost sitting back when she had it out with Calla at his place at freakin 3am dropped my respect for him a little <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. He definitely made up for it, but give me a break, he could have handled that better.<br /><br />Anyways, I liked seeing Cam and Avery, Jace and Teresa...they're great friends. The ending was a little open and didn't answer some questions, like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how will Jax and Calla work the long distance, and what will she do with her house? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm sure we'll find out in the next book, but this was on a whole quite disappointing for me, So 2 stars.</span>

Calla has had one heck of a messed up past, and the devastating impact of these circumstances has not only affected her emotionally but physically. Calla’s craptastic </span>
  <span id="freeText11906398847626671057" style="display:none"><b>2.5-3 No Totes Ma Goats Stars</b><br><br>Well I think the moral of the story here chitlens is<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492213104ra/22494321.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Because the dead-beat mama story line just completely overwhelmed, consumed, and I felt took away from this book. <b>Was this a drug story or a love story?</b> But once again, I will digress lol. So this story focuses on Calla, who is Teresa Hamilton’s BFF. Calla has had one heck of a messed up past, and the devastating impact of these circumstances has not only affected her emotionally but physically. Calla’s craptastic mama drained her bank account forcing her to come home over the summer. When she is trying to sort shit out, she meets Jax at her mom’s bar. Jax is your hot, bad boy, alpha that is immediately taken with Calla.<br><br>So that’s cool, I am thinking, broken heroine and broken alpha hero find each other, fix one another, HEA, bada boom bada bing. Umm..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412104298ra/11324598.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If that’s where the story stayed, I probably would have been ok, but shit just got like crazy weird. So you got a crazy mama, sure ok? If you care for a preview of the drama, enter here <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1st you’re stupid enough to stay at your mom’s old crack house, you let a guy come in and steal a couple mill of smack..oh then you get attacked at knife-point, kidnapped, punched in the face, dead body thrown on your front porch and add a couple of bullet holes to your gut. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I found myself skimming through those parts over and over.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492213104ra/22494322.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Then you have friends right? Side characters. Even they were too much. Katie, her crazy ass stripper friend?? That’s where totes ma goats came from. Who says that? Don’t ever say that, like ever. That’s right up there with <i>“moist” </i> on shit you don’t say unless you want to get smacked or something.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412104798ra/11324653.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Entering ex-gf drama..ok the ex-gf or ex-hookup still wants your man? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jax lets his ex continuously touch him, rub on him. He humors her way too much. Come over at 3am?? Sure why not, but you better call first. I am not kidding, he actually says that. The excuse was he is a nice guy? Really? Then he gets mad at Calla for being jealous, insinuating that her inexperience is to blame here. Sorry, if someone was touching my man, you better run bitch, no joke.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I felt, overall, this book had too much going on. And somehow, with an overload of crap, it felt very slow and long, dunno. No one will ever top Cam for me, ever, thus why if there is more to this series, maybe a book about Raphael and Michelangelo, I will not continue on. Unfortunately, this was not for me. I, ultimately, could not connect with either of the MC’s. The book did have some hot scenes but not enough to bring up the rating. I just thought it was meh, ok.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1082915057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1082915057" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1082915057?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=white-people-kissing">white-people-kissing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082915057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10201026240053877303"><b>
  <i>Today marks a day that I thought would never come... Thought would never happen... Today is the day I read a Jla book and didn't love it. </i>
</b> This book had me saying "<i>What the F am I reading</i>" at least once every chapter.<br/><br/>We have my first issue and that's Calla,the tormented girl with the dark past. Then there's my second problem, Jax, the slore turned nice guy. And then there's my final issue, the whole plot line. Calla is boring, cliche, and uninteresting in every since of the word. She often d</span>
  <span id="freeText10201026240053877303" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Today marks a day that I thought would never come... Thought would never happen... Today is the day I read a Jla book and didn't love it. </i>
</b> This book had me saying "<i>What the F am I reading</i>" at least once every chapter.<br><br>We have my first issue and that's Calla,the tormented girl with the dark past. Then there's my second problem, Jax, the slore turned nice guy. And then there's my final issue, the whole plot line. Calla is boring, cliche, and uninteresting in every since of the word. She often describes herself as dumb, and I have to agree. I thought she was. Jax looks-wise is all you'll ever want in a man. He even comes with a sexy back story. But that's pretty much all I liked about him. That and he said "<i>Honey" </i>a lot, which I found oddly sexy. Besides that I didn't connect with either characters. Jennifer writes characters that time and time again I've fallen in love with, and if this was any other writer I would have given this book a lower ranting and thrown into my DNF file. Everything from the way they met, to the secrets that "build" their relationship was a big turn off for me. Found it all rather tacky.<br><br>Jax from the start, though hot, is gross. He basically just short of pulls out his P on the girl and verbally assault her to get her into him. Yes he turns out to be more likeable by the end but not a whole like more. I think the whole "my face has a scar" thing with Calla was taken WAY to far! It was brought up, one too many times aka every two seconds. I also think I saw someone say that it was too highlighted that Calla must look like this blushing virgin, and I think that description hits the nail on the head. She is this super good girl whose never done anything with her life. Ya girls never even eaten pie... Like come on B they sell that at publix and I know you work near a Walmart and there's not a single one of those that isn't a super store now... Go to the Deli section and get yourself a pie and stop crying!<br><br>Then there's the intro of these random characters that are even more pointless than this plot line. <br>Aimee, Jax sorta Ex, only exists to make Calla jealous, me angry, and as a failed attempt at a plot twist. There are with that plot twist other failed plot twist, <b>THAT YOU WILL SEE COMING FROM A MILE AWAY!!!!</b> The whole story is a bunch of thrown together small stories, that try to build this bigger crazy story, but then falls flat on it's face. Also sidenote: there was no real point in her mom, you really could have completely erased any and everything about her and the story would have held up the same. Everything about this story to me just didn't play out well.<b> Jla has finally let me down, and it freaking sucks! <br><br><div>
<br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-r2YEx3ZbtqA/VM1gmhiiTMI/AAAAAAAABIE/QnXDKq_9jAI/s1600/nojustno.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422746407ra/13541438.gif" height="157" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div>
<br><br>This is the book I'm just going to straight pretend Jla didn't write. If someone mentions it I'm going to play Calla and be super clueless and naive. I'm all up for girls relying somewhat on a man (IN STORIES!!!) but when all is said and done I like my leading ladies standing on their own two feet with no one holding them up. Calla could have been this character, but instead <b>needed </b>the semi stalker Jax to do her work for her. Sigh just Sigh. <br><br><b>READ THIS REVIEW AND MORE OVER ON OUR BLOG!:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a></b></b></span>

</a><br><br>Calla Fritz is a 21 yr. old college student living in Shepherdstown, West Virginia attending Shepherd University. She is working on getting her degree in nursing &amp; is close to graduating. Calla has lived a sheltered life, and has no experience with guys. As a result she is a bit boy crazy. She's never had a boyfriend, been on dates, or been in a relationship. She's never even been kissed. She has a scar on her face, and doesn't think she's beautiful anymore. Guys are always her friend and nothing more.<br><br><a href="http://s993.photobucket.com/user/dalaa158/media/13d717af-91a7-4d0c-bf9d-83f07cac9ed9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Calla is all about her goals. She wants to finish college &amp; get a great job, &amp; have the life she's always dreamed of. She's lived a hard life and has tried to get as far away from her past as possible. Unfortunately her past catches up with her when her tuition check bounces &amp; all her money is gone. Her mom steals her money and she has to return to the small town she grew up in to try to fix the mess she's in. Her life severely veers off course when she arrives at her mom's bar Mona's, and her mom is MIA. She isn't sure what to do. She has no money, and all the sudden her perfectly planned future is up in the air.<br><br><a href="http://s993.photobucket.com/user/dalaa158/media/9e8c4084-fd17-468f-93cc-da20c263ce3e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>When Calla arrives at Mona's she meets a hot bartender named Jackson James aka Jax. He is stunningly beautiful, and is one of the sexiest guys she's ever seen, even if he is a little bossy. Calla is practically drooling all over this yummy man, &amp; is shocked when he openly is checking her out &amp; flirting with her. He makes it very clear how attracted he is to her, and Calla can't believe this gorgeous man wants her. Calla shares her first kiss with Jax, and he makes her feel beautiful!<br><br><a href="http://s993.photobucket.com/user/dalaa158/media/f46d9264-e2c4-4085-beb9-8adb28f10ccf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>We get some drama when bad guys that are after her mom set their sights on Calla. Jax will do anything to protect her &amp; falls hard for her. I really enjoyed this one &amp; thought Jax was absolutely delicious!!! :D<br><br><a href="http://s993.photobucket.com/user/dalaa158/media/1c5cdaa4-3fa5-46f8-9fb4-827525296331.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

Are you finally getting it?"<br><br>-"No. I think you really like me."<br><br>-"Yeah, babe, I really like you."<br><br>-The kiss...it was wet and deep and it wasn't good or nice. It was great and everything the romance books claimed kisses were. Jax tasted me. There were no other words to describe that kind of kiss.<br><br>-The kiss was sweet, it was careful and gentle. The tender sweep of his lips reached right down into my chest and squeezed my heart.<br><br>-I felt something else- something I hadn't felt in years. I felt cared for...cherished.<br><br>-God, I was so gone for him.</span>
